Annual Meeting of the British Chamber of Commerce and the China Association: Encouraging British Commercial Activities and Commenting on Chinese Politics

The Shanghai British Chamber of Commerce and the China Association branch in China held their 21st annual meeting at the Shanghai Club at 5:15 PM on Thursday, the 16th. The meeting was chaired by Mr. Marshall, Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce. In addition to members, attendees included Sir Brenan, British Consul-General in Shanghai and Honorary President of the Chamber of Commerce, Mr. Peel, Commercial Counsellor of the British Embassy, Mr. Hude Hai, Chairman of the China Association, Mr. Ma Sai, Vice Chairman, and other prominent figures. First, Mr. Marshall read the annual report of the Chamber of Commerce, which was quite lengthy. It began with condolences on the passing of King George V of England, expressing confidence that the new monarch, Edward VII, would inherit his predecessor's ambitions. Then, it discussed the political situation in China last year and the impact of the political upheaval in North China, praising Generalissimo Chiang's efforts in suppressing the communists and hoping for an early unification of the North and South. It stated that in 1935, no major internal political unrest disrupted commerce, and therefore, the decline in commerce that year was largely due to the efforts of foreigners, on the one hand, and the recall of silver and the instability in North China, on the other. It then mentioned the losses from the floods in the Yellow River and Yangtze River last summer, which amounted to 450 million yuan. It also stated that foreign trade in China last year decreased by 70 million yuan compared to 1934 and 462 million yuan compared to 1932. The total import and export trade was compared in a table in millions of yuan, as follows:

1933 1934 1935

Net Imports 1,345 1,030 919

Exports 612 535 576

Total 1,957 1,565 1,495

Trade Deficit 733 495 343

The decrease in trade volume was partly due to the increase in local manufactured goods, but also due to the lack of confidence caused by political instability and the aggression in North China. It then discussed the harmful effects of smuggling in the demilitarized zone of North China on Chinese and foreign commerce. It also mentioned the increase and decrease of various imported and exported goods. In 1935, the export of Chinese raw silk greatly increased, but this was due to the Japanese restrictions on purchases in the spring and summer of that year and the subsequent damage to autumn purchases. China cannot rely on this favorable situation for long and should strive to improve standards and breeding methods. Attention should also be paid to tea cultivation methods. Government promotion can greatly increase foreign demand for Chinese tea. It also stated that Britain's trade with China had fallen from third to fourth place, with the order being the United States, Japan, Germany, and Britain. However, if the British Empire, including Hong Kong, is included, it still ranks first, followed by the United States, then Japan, and then Germany. British merchants naturally regret that British import trade has fallen to fourth place, but the remedy is not something that British people in China can do. It depends on domestic manufacturers. Price and favorable credit terms are important factors in obtaining orders. Unless efforts are made to compete with other countries on price and terms, Britain's position is unlikely to improve. This is not to say to take unnecessary risks, but to say that when there is adequate assurance, the convenience of credit should be given careful consideration. It then mentioned that the adoption of the legal tender and the stabilization of exchange rates were beneficial to merchants and export trade, and the new nickel and copper coins were welcomed by all parties. If the stability of the legal tender can be maintained for a long time, and standard new coins can be issued steadily, it can greatly contribute to the prosperity of commerce. It also mentioned the progress of Chinese industry in recent years, stating that heavy industry and public utilities requiring large amounts of capital should be operated by the authorities. However, some provincial and municipal governments are now engaged in light industry, which is not a good example, as it inhibits the development of private enterprise and creates monopolies. Government operation of such enterprises is harmful to the people and not beneficial. It then mentioned the achievements of Chinese railways and highways last year, stating that the overdue payments of Chinese railway loans are now being addressed, which will greatly facilitate future railway loans. It criticized the stamp tax law promulgated in China last year and other measures that hinder foreign commerce. It then mentioned the achievements of the National Economic Council last year in rural reconstruction, cooperative societies, agricultural development, and other undertakings, as well as the establishment of the Sino-British Trade Association. Finally, it summarized the entire report, stating that although commerce was in an unfavorable situation last year, much of the situation in North China, the so-called autonomous movement, and smuggling in the demilitarized zone were beyond the control of the Chinese authorities. Despite these unfavorable conditions, China's achievements in many areas were still remarkable. Without the instability caused by the northern forces, the future would be promising. However, given the current situation, the future is not yet optimistic. The report then listed the work of the Chamber of Commerce during the year. After the report, Sir Brenan and Mr. Peel delivered speeches. Mr. Peel said that British commerce is now on the road to recovery. He expects China to enter an era of importation and development, its currency management is gradually becoming stable, and its industrial revitalization is progressing in an orderly manner without being hasty, which is commendable. British merchants are prepared and willing to help China's future commercial progress, as in the past. The meeting then approved the accounts for the year and elected twelve new and old directors. Then, the meeting of the China Association was convened, and Chairman Hude Hai read the report, which stated that major issues between China and Britain, such as consular jurisdiction and the recovery of concessions, have been stalled since the end of 1931. However, one day these issues will be raised again, and the British should pay constant attention to the fact that when they are raised again in the future, the British Foreign Office and the British Embassy should allow the opinions of the British community in Shanghai to have adequate participation. The main task of the two associations in peacetime should be to jointly resist the continuous attempts to discriminate against foreign interests. The report cited the continued acceptance of the International Savings Society by the Chinese authorities as evidence of discrimination against foreign interests. It went on to say that the various laws enacted in recent years, such as the Encouragement of Industry Law, the Insurance Law, and the Private Railway Law, all directly discriminate against foreign interests and are contrary to the Chinese authorities' desire to encourage foreign investment. It then discussed the stamp tax, business tax, and other taxes, saying that on the surface, they were adopted in accordance with Western principles and, with the approval of the treaty powers, could be easily applied to foreigners. However, these laws cannot be applied to Chinese people, because local authorities in various provinces still enact their own laws, which run parallel to the laws promulgated by the central government. There are many troubles with taxes on taxes, which make it impossible for many foreign businesses to operate. We do not want to argue with the Chinese government's efforts to reform the laws. The only safe principle to be followed is the one stated in Chamberlain's note of January 1927, that the British government is prepared to have the British community in China pay legitimate taxes, that is, taxes paid by all Chinese citizens alike. This principle cannot be limited to taxes, but should also be applied to factory laws and the like, so as to avoid differences in treatment between Chinese and foreigners. In recent years, China's credit has made it difficult to make progress, but there are still many debts that are overdue. The resulting bad impression cannot be eliminated by excluding foreign businesses in China. The two associations cannot ignore the various situations mentioned above, and only cooperation, not discrimination, can greatly benefit China's interests and the interests of British merchants and investors in China. After the report, the association approved the accounts for the year and elected three new directors, and the meeting was adjourned.

The Chinese Ratepayers' Association Will Continue Its General Meeting Today to Elect One Chinese Committee Member and 27 Executive Committee Members

The Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession will continue its 15th First Delegates' Meeting at 2:00 PM today at 59 Hong Kong Road. Notices have been sent to all delegates to attend on time. Four Radio Stations Are Being Built, Materials Have Been Shipped from England and Distributed to Various Locations for Installation

According to Da Gong She, the long-distance telephone network connecting the nine provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Shandong, Hebei, Henan, Hubei, and Hunan, was planned by the Long-Distance Telephone Administration of the Ministry of Communications in January 1934. Five main lines were designated: Nanjing to Hankou, Nanjing to Tianjin, Xuzhou to Zhengzhou, Hankou to Changsha, and Jinan to Qingdao. The completed sections include (Jinghan Line) Nanjing to Shun'an, Hukou, Yangxin, Jinghan Branch Line, Yinjiahui, Shun'an to Anqing, (Jingjin Line) Nanjing to Xuzhou, Xuzhou to Jinan, (Hanxiang Line) Hankou to Changsha, Xuzhou to Kaifeng and Zhengzhou. The sections under construction include (Jingjin Line) Jinan to Tianjin, Tianjin to Beijing Branch Line, and (Jiqing Line) Jinan to Qingdao and various counties.

Building Radio Stations

In order to make the sound of long-distance calls clear across the country, boost radio wave power, and prevent the impact of hurricanes and rain, the Ministry of Communications is building radio stations in Shanghai, Nanjing, Jiujiang, Hankou, and other places. The materials are ordered from the British Standard Electric Company by the Ministry of Communications' electrical materials supply department, costing more than 200,000 yuan. The materials have now been shipped from England to Shanghai and transferred to the Nanjing National Long-Distance Telephone Administration Bureau for distribution to various locations for installation. The radio station in Shanghai will be attached to the long-distance telephone station on Yongxing Road in Zhabei.

Telephone Service in June

In recent years, after the Ministry of Communications ordered the telephone bureaus in various provinces and cities to work hard on telephone construction, the national telephone area has reached more than 600 locations. In addition to the telegraph and telephone lines, the total length of the telephone lines, including the newly built long-distance telephone lines in nine provinces, is more than 9,200 kilometers. Transportation is becoming more and more convenient, and the business is developing more and more, almost replacing telegrams. The long-distance telephone project across the nine provinces has been delayed due to weather conditions and will be completed by the end of next month. The completed sections are currently being tested separately, and it is expected that the telephone service will be open in early June of this year. At that time, the Ministry of Communications will hold a grand telephone ceremony in Beijing, and the Minister of Communications will report on the construction process.

The Special District Rickshaw Association Asks to Increase the Number of Registered Rickshaw Pullers, Sending Letters to the Municipal Council and Requesting Assistance from the Chinese Directors, and Issuing Notices to Rickshaw Owners to Resolve to Persevere to the End

According to Xin Sheng She, the Special District Rickshaw Association sent letters to the Municipal Council and the Chinese Directors yesterday regarding the registration of rickshaw pullers by the Municipal Council and issued notices to rickshaw owners. The following is a record:

Letter to the Municipal Council The Special District Rickshaw Association previously sent a letter to the Municipal Council, expressing its unwillingness to pay the mutual aid fee and its dissatisfaction with the mutual aid society, considering the mutual aid society to be a business of the Municipal Council. The issue of its existence or abolition should be decided by rickshaw merchants and rickshaw pullers. However, the Municipal Council's reply did not mention the mutual aid fee. Therefore, yesterday, lawyer Gu Wo sent a letter to the Municipal Council, requesting a meeting of rickshaw merchant representatives to resolve all outstanding issues. The original text reads, "We have just received your letter of the 9th of this month and have already informed our clients. Our clients express deep regret over the rickshaw puller disturbances and declare that they have absolutely no involvement in the disturbances. Our clients received a letter from the Rickshaw Affairs Committee on the 7th of this month and immediately published it in the newspaper on Sunday to inform all rickshaw owners that rickshaw puller registration will continue from the 14th of this month. However, because the Rickshaw Committee only stipulates an increase of 5,000 rickshaw puller registrations, the number is very small. Our clients have long believed that the number of rickshaw pullers needed for the rickshaw industry is insufficient, and it is difficult to allocate a small number of registrations to a large number of rickshaw pullers who have not been registered. Your council's letter of the 9th stated that the Rickshaw Committee has been authorized to issue rickshaw puller registration certificates sufficient for the needs of the rickshaw industry. However, the rickshaw pullers demanded registration yesterday and caused disturbances, which is obviously because the Rickshaw Committee is unwilling to issue rickshaw puller registration certificates sufficient for the needs of the rickshaw industry. The Rickshaw Committee has not yet clearly stipulated the number of rickshaw pullers who should be registered to meet the needs of the rickshaw industry or obtained a definite number agreed to by the Rickshaw Merchants' Association. In order to avoid further disturbances by rickshaw pullers, our clients hope that the matters mentioned in the two letters of the 26th and 30th of last month, which were not mentioned in your council's reply of the 9th of this month, namely the collection of mutual aid fees and the issue of the existence or abolition of the mutual aid society, should be resolved as soon as possible by convening a joint meeting of rickshaw merchant representatives and your council representatives. In accordance with the intentions expressed in the unresolved paragraphs of your council's letter, our clients are very willing to have an opportunity to personally present everything to your council."

Letter to the Chinese Directors The association sent a letter to the Chinese directors, saying, "We respectfully inform you that upon reading the newspapers, we learned that Mr. has been re-elected as a Chinese director in the 15th Delegates' Meeting of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Concession, which shows that he enjoys popular support and the enthusiasm of the citizens of the city in unanimously supporting him. We are deeply impressed. In recent years, the rickshaw disputes in the Public Concession have been caused by a part of the foreigners who want to eliminate rickshaws in order to realize the monopoly of foreign-run transportation businesses. Since the establishment of the Rickshaw Affairs Committee, which represents this kind of economic aggression, a year has passed, and it has been picking on the rickshaw industry in every possible way, exhausting its ability to demand perfection. Therefore, the rickshaw industry has plummeted in the past two years and is becoming increasingly precarious, and the livelihoods of rickshaw pullers have also suffered a great blow. For example, on April 14, the restriction of registration for unemployed rickshaw pullers by the Rickshaw Committee led to a conflict and bloodshed incident, which is very painful to say. It is understood that there are 10,000 rickshaws and 70,000 to 80,000 rickshaw pullers in the Public Concession. Since the Rickshaw Committee registered more than 41,000 rickshaw pullers in the previous year, there are as many as 30,000 to 40,000 rickshaw pullers who are unemployed because they are not registered and cannot pull rickshaws. Considering the livelihood of the poor, our association has repeatedly requested the Municipal Council to continue registration to save tens of thousands of unemployed people. Fortunately, we were invited to allow the registration to continue from April 14. Unexpectedly, the Rickshaw Committee temporarily announced that it would restrict one person to be introduced for every two rickshaws, with a total of 5,000 people. There is not enough porridge for everyone, which caused a conflict between rickshaw pullers and patrols. It is a deep regret. Since the purpose of rickshaw puller registration is to protect rickshaw pullers, it should be registered as much as possible according to the actual needs to avoid regrets. However, the Rickshaw Committee ignores the facts and restricts 5,000 people, so that most rickshaw pullers are still unemployed because they cannot register. This kind of action is tantamount to cutting off the livelihood of rickshaw pullers, which is inappropriate in terms of both emotion and reason. We have always admired Mr.'s enthusiasm for safeguarding Chinese commerce and caring for the livelihoods of the poor. We respectfully request that you strive for unrestricted rickshaw puller registration at the current board of directors' meeting so that tens of thousands of unemployed rickshaw pullers can maintain their lives. We rely entirely on Mr.'s contribution. We are eagerly awaiting your response."

Notice to Rickshaw Owners The industry association issued a notice to all rickshaw owners yesterday, saying, "To all rickshaw owners, the rickshaw industry is unfortunate and has been repeatedly ravaged. The reduction of rickshaw rent, the mandatory replacement of rickshaw styles, the implementation of rickshaw puller registration, and the payment of mutual aid fees are all enough to bankrupt our rickshaw industry. Although we rickshaw merchants initially compromised for the sake of peace and endured insults, we can never satisfy the insatiable ambitions of economic aggressors. In the past two years, the business of rickshaw merchants has plummeted, and the livelihoods of rickshaw pullers are in imminent danger. It is very painful to say. We read in the newspapers that in the speech by Arnold, the Director-General of the Municipal Council, at the annual meeting of the Western Ratepayers' Association on April 15, the foreigners' ambition to eliminate rickshaws was completely exposed. All the issues of reducing rickshaw rents and registering rickshaw pullers are transitional issues. Its ultimate goal is to fundamentally eliminate rickshaws in order to realize the monopoly of foreign-run buses and trams. Such ambition is appalling. At this critical juncture of life and death, in order to seek the survival of the rickshaw industry, we must rely on the unity of all rickshaw merchants and rickshaw pullers to jointly resist foreign aggression. If there is a lack of solidarity and small gains are seen while ignoring the big picture, then we can only bring about our own destruction. It will be too late to regret it at that time. Therefore, we sincerely inform you that all our rickshaw owners must unite with the greatest determination and spirit, act in unison, and share life and death. Then, there may be a glimmer of hope for the future of the rickshaw industry. This is a heartfelt and loyal message. We hope you will understand."

The Husband and Wife Encounter a Mishap

Zhou Keming, a 34-year-old from Fenghua, lives at 1407 Luzon Road in this city. In his early years, he married a woman named Sun from the same town. The couple has always been extremely harmonious. However, because Zhou was doing business in Harbin, he did not return home for several years. This time, he has been away from home for more than two years since the winter of 1934. Unexpectedly, Sun's abdomen has recently been swelling. After a doctor's examination, it was said that she was four months pregnant. At that time, a carpenter named Zou Asheng happened to be present in the doctor's office. Zou was Sun's neighbor and was usually a busybody. Hearing the news that the empty house had suddenly become pregnant after two years, he spread the news everywhere, which eventually reached Zhou's ears. Zhou was usually impatient and, without asking the details, immediately accused Sun of infidelity in a letter. Sun, at this moment of unexpected good fortune, was looking forward to his return when she suddenly received this letter and was overwhelmed with grief. Fortunately, after Sun's cousin, Sun Shiyao, accompanied her to Dr. Wang Longxiang for a detailed diagnosis, it was determined that Sun was weak and depressed and had amenorrhea. She then purchased "Yuè Yuè Hóng" and "Female Treasure" from a large pharmacy and took them according to the instructions on the package insert. Now, she has indeed had her period, and her body has recovered. It is said that Zhou arrived in Shanghai yesterday, intending to investigate the affair and prepare to file for divorce. However, after being told the truth by others, he is now relieved and free of suspicion, and they are as loving as ever.

Fish Market Announces - Abundant Fish Production in the Sijiao Islands

The Sijiao Islands, located at the mouth of the Yangtze River, are the most abundant fish-producing area in our country. Statistics show that the value of aquatic products produced annually exceeds ten million yuan. The Ministry of Industry's Fish Market sent personnel to investigate and published the following information on the island's important fisheries:

Island Formation The Sijiao Islands are a general term for a group of islands, divided into the Ma'an Islands, Baker Islands, and Luanxing Islands. Among them, the islands of Dashan and Sijiao in the Ma'an Islands have the largest area and are important bases for fisheries. The aquatic products produced nearby are constantly breeding and multiplying, making it the most abundant marine product area in our country. Among the most famous products are large yellow croaker, yellow croaker, cuttlefish, and ribbonfish.

Annual Production The total annual fish production of the island is approximately 4,292,100 dan, with a value of approximately 2,215,000 yuan. This includes over 2 million dan of yellow croaker, worth 3,000,000 yuan; over 600,000 dan of large yellow croaker, worth 2,400,000 yuan; over 500,000 dan of cuttlefish, worth 2,000,000 yuan; over 1 million dan of ribbonfish, worth 2,000,000 yuan; over 100,000 dan of pufferfish, worth 800,000 yuan; over 8,000 dan of Spanish mackerel, worth 100,000 yuan; over 500 dan of pomfret, worth 20,000 yuan; 2,000 dan of sole, worth 30,000 yuan; over 20,000 dan of swimming crab, worth 160,000 yuan; over 10,000 dan of dried jellyfish, worth 120,000 yuan; 18,000 dan of abalone, worth 270,000 yuan; over 2,000 dan of dried mussels, worth 70,000 yuan; 1,000 dan of seaweed, worth 100,000 yuan; over 600 dan of dried sea swallow, worth 45,000 yuan; 10,000 dan of shrimp, worth 40,000 yuan; and over 10,000 dan of miscellaneous fish, worth 60,000 yuan.

City Chamber of Commerce Instructions - Stamp Tax Method for Housing Tickets and Land Deeds

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to Huaxing Rice Store yesterday, providing instructions on the stamp tax method for housing tickets: "Regarding your inquiry about housing tickets, the tax rate for silver receipts is as follows: one cent for monthly rent of three yuan, two cents for rent of ten yuan, and three cents for rent of one hundred yuan or more. As for the lease agreement on the rental book, which is signed and stamped by the tenant, the tenant is the party establishing the agreement, and the tenant is responsible for paying the stamp tax. The stamp tax on the rental amount stated in the lease agreement is two cents for every ten yuan. For amounts less than ten yuan, according to item 10 of the tax rate table, the tax is exempt. As for the land deed for absolute sale, because the land deed requires the payment of deed tax, according to Article 3, paragraph 2 of the Stamp Tax Law, this type of land deed does not need to be stamped."

Fragrance Industry Workers Went on Strike Yesterday Morning - To Support Workers at the Dayuan Ship Fragrance Factory

According to Dagong News, the Dayuan Ship Fragrance Factory in the British Concession on Hualei Road recently experienced sluggish business. The originally stipulated wage for resuming work was reduced from $0.521 to $0.48 per day with the consent of the workers. However, the factory recently reduced the wage again to $0.40 per day, causing dissatisfaction among the workers, who requested assistance from the Shanghai Fragrance Industry Workers Union. After the union's negotiations, no results were achieved. All the workers in the industry went on strike yesterday in response. Yesterday afternoon at 3 PM, a general meeting of all members was held at the union hall, attended by over 350 people. It was resolved to propose the following preconditions: 1) The factory must earnestly fulfill the labor-management contract. 2) The original wage must be restored. 3) Wages must be paid as usual during the strike. 4) The factory must not indiscriminately recruit apprentices. 5) The factory must not arbitrarily dismiss workers in the future.

Silkworm Moth Factory - Accountant Stabbed to Death - A Knife Wound to the Neck Severed the Throat

Chen Baolin (49 years old, from Ningbo), the accountant of the Yuanchang Silk Thread Factory (also known as the Silkworm Moth Factory) at No. 2 Tanjiaqiao, Zhabei, was found stabbed to death in the factory's kitchen yesterday morning around 6 AM. There was a knife wound of more than four inches in length on his neck which severed his throat. He lay in a pool of blood. After he was discovered, the report was made to Officer Yang Shoushen of the No. 51 guard post of the Tanjiaqiao Police Station, who went to investigate. The police station was notified, and a further investigation was conducted. A murder weapon (a kitchen knife) was found. The local guarantor was instructed to report to the Shanghai District Court for an autopsy. At about 5 PM, Prosecutor Lei Binzhang and others arrived to examine the scene and determined that the deceased, Chen Baolin, had died from a stab wound sustained while he was alive. Fellow workers Zhu Lanlin (41 years old, from Haimen), Zhu Guocheng (37 years old, from Haimen), Lu Erbao (37 years old, from Haimen), and Zhang Boshu (62 years old, from Shaoxing) were summoned to the scene and briefly questioned. Zhan Dayou's Property Dispute - Zhan Yunshan and Others Convicted of Forging Documents

Zhan Daoyou, the owner of the Zhan Dayou Farm, had only one daughter, who married Zha Qilin. Zhan Daoyou passed away in 1929, leaving behind over two million yuan in property. However, his daughter, Zha Zhan, also died. Zha Zhan had two sons and one daughter, who inherited their maternal grandfather's estate in succession, with Zha Qilin as their guardian. Zhan Yunsan and Zhan Songsan, Zhan Daoyou's younger brothers, filed a lawsuit in the Civil Court of the District Court against Zha Qilin, requesting an audit. They then filed a lawsuit claiming inheritance, alleging that Daoyou had adopted Yunsan's son as his son and produced a certificate of adoption and a will allegedly written by Zhan Daoyou. They also brought Daoyou's nephew, Yu Ruizhi, to court as a witness to verify the document. Zha Qilin claimed that the documents were forged. The judge submitted them for authentication, and they were indeed found to be forged. They were reported to the prosecutor, who filed a public prosecution. After repeated trials and arguments, Judge Cai announced the verdict yesterday. Zhan Yunsan and Zhan Songsan were jointly sentenced to four months of imprisonment for using forged private documents. Yu Ruizhi was sentenced to two months of imprisonment for assisting in forging private documents and four months for making false statements under oath during the trial. The total sentence to be served was five months of imprisonment.

Grain Council Plan: Building New-Style Granaries to Store Grain

Exemption of Full Tax on Imported Broken Rice Requested; Ningbo Chamber of Commerce Changes Plan to Purchase Imported Rice

Yesterday morning, a reporter from the New Voice News Agency visited Mr. Gu Xin-yi, a leader in the grain industry, to inquire about various grain-related matters. Mr. Gu provided the following information:

**Cessation of Imported Rice Orders**

The Shanghai Grain Council, through its 43rd regular meeting, resolved to request the Social Affairs Bureau to forward a request to the Municipal Government for an appropriation of 200,000 yuan to order 100,000 bags of imported rice. The remaining funds were to be secured upon arrival of the rice. Simultaneously, it requested the Ministry of Finance to issue a tax exemption permit. However, due to the Municipal Government's financial difficulties, no funds were available. Moreover, although Shanghai experienced a grain shortage during this pre-harvest period, it was not expected to become a major problem. Therefore, the proposal to order imported rice has been discontinued.

**Plan to Build New-Style Granaries**

Regarding the Duojialu base of the original Shanghai grain storage funds and properties rented by Shanghai hospitals, it was resolved to request the Social Affairs Bureau to forward a reasoned argument to the Municipal Government, insisting that grain storage funds and properties should not be used for other purposes in accordance with central government directives. Furthermore, it requested the Municipal Government to allocate funds to build new-style granaries on the original site to handle grain storage matters. Implementation measures have now been determined, and construction is planned to reserve grain.

**Exemption of Increased Tax on Broken Rice Requested**

Since the Customs announcement on April 11th to levy full tax on broken rice, grain merchants had ordered a total of over 100,000 bags of broken rice before April 11th that had not yet been imported. The guild has resolved through a meeting to send a letter from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to the Executive Yuan's Ministry of Finance Customs Administration, requesting that broken rice traded before April 11th still be taxed at half the rate. However, since the full tax was levied, grain merchants have no longer ordered imported broken rice.

**Ningbo Changes Plan to Purchase Imported Rice**

Previously, the Ningbo Chamber of Commerce, in view of the approximately 300,000 shi shortage of rice in the area this year, borrowed 3 million yuan from the Farmers Bank of China to order 300,000 bags of imported rice and requested the Executive Yuan to issue a free permit. Now, the original plan has been changed to order 40,000 to 50,000 bags of imported broken rice, which has already been traded and will arrive in China successively. This broken rice was ordered before April 11th, and they are currently requesting exemption from full tax upon import.

Rickshaw Puller Conflict with Police: Lost Handgun Recovered, Hidden in Rickshaw Puller Qian Fu-sheng's Bedroom; Police Charge with Robbery and Grievous Bodily Harm

Between 9:00 AM and 12:00 PM on the 14th of this month, a conflict occurred between rickshaw pullers and police officers in the area of McTyeire Road and Shunde Road due to rickshaw registration. At the time, in addition to Chinese Deputy Head Constable Tao Shi-wei being injured, Chinese Constable No. 1853 was also seriously injured, and a handgun with six bullets that he was carrying was stolen. Although the police subsequently arrested many rioters and sent them to the court for interrogation and detention, the person who actually robbed the gun and bullets had not been captured. Therefore, in recent days, the police authorities have paid close attention to this case and ordered all police stations to investigate strictly. On the morning of the day before yesterday at about 1:00 AM, Chinese detectives Zhou Hong-lin and Qian Xian-ting of the Public Concession Police Headquarters learned that the suspect in the handgun robbery case was hiding at No. 10 Chongde Lane, Hengfeng Road, Zhabei. They reported this to Inspector Lu Lian-kui, who ordered Detective Song Bing-zheng and Western Detective White to go to the address together with detectives from the Zhabei Public Security Bureau. They found that No. 10 Chongde Lane was a rickshaw repair company. The kitchen shed was the bedroom of Qian Fu-sheng, a rickshaw puller from Ningbo. They searched the room and found the stolen handgun and six bullets of Chinese Constable No. 1853 on a broken rickshaw, covered with Qian Fu-sheng's clothes. They arrested Qian Fu-sheng and questioned him about the origin of the handgun, but he claimed he didn't know and needed to ask Zhu San. The detectives then apprehended Zhu San (i.e., Zhu Shou-fu), who also gave evasive answers and refused to speak clearly. They were both taken to the Public Security Bureau and then transferred to the Xinza Police Station for detention. Yesterday morning, police lawyer Zhang Tian-yin sent them to the Eighth Criminal Division of the First Special District Court, charging them with robbery and grievous bodily harm under Article 328, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Law. He also recounted the previous events, saying that the injured victim, Chinese Constable No. 1853, was seriously injured, with severe eye damage, and was still being treated in the hospital. Therefore, he requested an extension. Qian Fu-sheng and Zhu Shou-fu both claimed that they did not know who had placed the handgun on the rickshaw. After Judge Tan Xin-zhen verified the confession, he ordered the two defendants to be detained pending a further hearing in seven days.

The weather in the city has been quite hot recently, especially on the day before yesterday (the 16th). Residents are mostly dressed in light clothing, and even laborers working with bare arms are sweating profusely. Unexpectedly, after nightfall, a gust of wind suddenly rose, howling all night. Coal Industry Attention: Another New Coal Firm Lawsuit; Over a Hundred People Attended Hearing Yesterday; Guild Secretary Recounts Handling of Stolen Coal; New Coal Admits Coal Purchased from Mitsui

The Liu Jiang Coal Mine in Hebei Province has been seized by force, and negotiations for its return have been unsuccessful for a long time. The Liu Jiang Coal Mine Company reported this to the Shanghai Coal Industry Guild, which resolved to refuse to sell Liu Jiang coal; violators would have their membership in the Coal Industry Guild revoked and face economic sanctions. Zhang Yan-zhang, the owner of the New Coal Firm, a Ningbo native and currently a supervisory committee member of the Coal Industry Guild, also supported the above resolution when it was passed. However, he later went back on his word and was the first to violate the resolution by purchasing a large quantity of Liu Jiang coal and dumping it at a low price. The Liu Jiang Company then claimed that he was selling stolen coal and requested the Coal Industry Guild to implement sanctions based on the resolution. Zhang Yan-zhang then filed a criminal self-accusation with the First Special District Local Court against Shen Jin-zhou, the manager of Liu Jiang, for obstructing credit. The case has been heard twice, as reported in previous newspapers. Currently, Zhang Yan-zhang has successively filed petitions requesting that Liu Hong-sheng, Chen Yu-tang, Wei Hong-wen, Mao Chun-pu, Pan Yi-san, and five others be added as defendants in the case. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ye Sheng-chao continued the hearing. The defendant was still only Shen Jin-zhou, who appeared in court. However, over a hundred people from the coal industry attended the hearing, making the Fifth Court crowded. The summoned witness, Wang Ping-nan, the secretary of the Coal Industry Guild, recounted the guild's handling of the matter, saying that Zhang was a supervisory committee member and Shen was an executive committee member. After Liu Jiang requested assistance, the guild held several executive committee or executive and supervisory committee joint meetings before resolving the sanctions against those who sold Liu Jiang coal. Zhang also stated at the meetings that anyone who sold Liu Jiang coal should be expelled from the guild. Unexpectedly, Zhang's New Coal Firm actually sold it, disguising it as Hebei coal. He then submitted all the relevant documents and drafts to the court for review. Zhang Yan-zhang testified that the coal was purchased from Mitsui, and Mitsui purchased it from Tai Kee Company. Tai Kee is one of the three major coal mines in Qinhuangdao. The defendant claimed it was stolen coal and should provide proof. Shen Jin-zhou stated that Tai Kee never ships coal to Shanghai, as all industry members know. The only coal from Qinhuangdao is Liu Jiang coal. The plaintiff's lawyer then requested to question the defendant about his lawsuit in eastern Hebei. The defendant's lawyer said that there was a puppet government in eastern Hebei, and it was painful to talk about it, so he did not elaborate. The court has ordered a further hearing next Friday afternoon. Suddenly, a voice came from the crowd of listeners, clamoring in response. The bailiffs and court police stopped it and ordered the audience to leave, and the order was fortunately not disrupted, but several Chinese and Western bailiffs and police officers had already gathered after hearing the sound, then all the idlers in the court dispersed.

Post Office Promotes Registered Express Delivery

In the past, the express mail service offered by post offices across China only included "registered express delivery," which was handled at designated post offices. In order to facilitate the public, the Ministry of Communications added "ordinary express mail" last year, which can be sent and received everywhere. It is now learned that the Directorate General of Posts is taking a further step to promote registered express delivery again. Except for Mongolia and Xinjiang, it can be delivered to any location without restrictions. When the post office sends it, it is delivered via the fastest route. After it arrives, it is also delivered using the fastest method, even if it is submitted after the ordinary mail dispatch time, it will be sent out as quickly as possible within the possible range. The plan has been ordered by the Directorate General of Posts to all post offices nationwide and will be implemented uniformly from May 1st.

According to Datong News Agency, the Ningbo Association in Shanghai sent a letter to the Jianghai Customs Commissioner, stating: "Respectfully, according to a letter from our member Ying Sun-chuan, our fellow townsman Lou A-he, 41 years old, from Duji Village, Jinxiang Township, Dinghai, had been engaged in fishing. On the morning of the 19th, when sailing to the waters off Zhushanmen, they were chased by Shanghai patrol boat No. 25. Fearing a misunderstanding, they immediately lowered the sails to await inspection. Only then did the foreigner realize that the shooting was inappropriate. They accompanied Lou A-he and the boat owner Zhu A-bao to the Dinghai Hospital for treatment. Due to the severity of the injuries, the Dinghai Hospital was unable to help. On the same day, patrol boat No. 25 transported him to the Ningbo Huamei Hospital. He eventually died at 3:00 PM on the 20th at Huamei Hospital due to his injuries. The Ningbo Customs purchased a coffin for him, and the Ningbo Customs Commissioner issued 20 yuan for travel expenses, which was received by Lou A-he's wife, Chen, and was verbally instructed to send a telegram to Jianghai Customs to request compensation. It has been more than a month since Lou A-he was killed, and compensation has not yet been issued. Regardless of whether the Ningbo Customs Commissioner fulfills his promise, it is justified that the patrol boat mistakenly injured the fisherman. Lou A-he's funeral was desolate, leaving behind a widow and orphan, making their livelihood extremely difficult. As our association is closer to the victim, we know the details thoroughly. Therefore, we provide a brief account of the incident and request that you find a way to negotiate and seek compensation for the victim to appease his spirit. We also hope to receive a reply." Addressed to the Jianghai Customs Commissioner.

Gu Zhu-xuan's Opium Dross and White Powder Tested to Have Narcotic Toxicity; Custodial Dereliction Case to Continue Hearing Today

Gu Zhu-xuan was arrested and sent to the Second Special District Court for instigating the assassination of Tang Jia-peng and was sentenced to 15 years in prison. During the appeal period, Gu bribed guards to instigate perjury, and the prosecutor filed a public prosecution for two closed hearings. At the same time, prison guard director Jia Fu-rong and detention center director Wu Lu were accused by inmates such as Li He-shang of colluding with Gu Zhu-xuan to smoke opium in the outer sick ward, and opium dross, white powder, and other items were confiscated. The court sent the confiscated opium slices and white powder to the Zhenru Forensic Institute to test for toxicity. It is now learned that the forensic institute has completed the test and the results show that the white powder, opium dross, and other items do contain narcotic toxicity. The court received the report a few days ago and has scheduled the head of the criminal court, Wang Gang-xu, to continue the hearing on the dereliction of duty case at 2:00 PM today.

Worthless Son-in-Law Opens Fire After Loan Request Denied; Wife and Mother-in-Law Both Injured

Mrs. Tang Qi, a local woman, 56 years old, lives at No. 1 Tangjiazhai, Caojiadu. She has a daughter named Yinzhu, currently 36 years old, who married Shen A-di, a local man, through a matchmaker many years ago. Unexpectedly, A-di has no regular job and roams around all day, associating with local ruffians, acting like a hooligan, specializing in meddling, and extorting money whenever possible. Occasionally, when he is short of money, he goes to his mother-in-law's house to borrow money from Tang Qi. If he is not satisfied, he often curses and scolds, causing the Tang family to fear him like a tiger and hate him to the core. In the end, he still manages to borrow some money and leaves. Yesterday afternoon at around 7:00 PM, Shen A-di, under the pretext of visiting his wife Yinzhu, who had not returned from Ningbo, went to her house. Before long, A-di's old habits returned, and he again asked his mother-in-law for a loan. Tang Qi refused outright and offered some advice, hoping he would change his ways and strive for self-reliance. However, A-di took the good advice as an insult and became extremely angry, cursing and scolding. At that time, Yinzhu could not bear it and helped her mother to confront A-di. Unexpectedly, Shen A-di said nothing, rushed out of the door, and brought back four hooligans, rushing into the inner room, pulling out a handgun, and shooting Tang Qi and Yinzhu in the legs each, then fleeing together. By the time the patrol police arrived after being notified, both the mother and daughter were lying on the ground, covered in blood. They quickly hired a car to take them to the hospital for treatment, and then reported to the police station, sending officers out to pursue and arrest the perpetrators.

Female Witch Arrested by Police

Zhu Ji, a woman from Taicang, 38 years old, lives upstairs at No. 1 Rongshan Lane, Singapore Road, in western Shanghai. She works as a female witch (commonly known as a "spiritual medium"), relying on false claims of ghosts and spirits to deceive ignorant and foolish people, and takes the opportunity to extort money. Over the years, many people have been deceived by her. Recently, her activities have become even more harmful. After receiving a tip-off, Inspector Li of the Singapore Road Public Security Substation, together with Sergeant Fa Jin-zhang and Constable Zhang Ru-lan, went to the address at around 5:00 PM yesterday and arrested the woman and her husband, Zhu Chang-sheng, 46 years old, from Suzhou. They also found a box of incense ashes, two Buddhist idols, and six paper gods in the house and took them all to the station for questioning.

Kidnapping Ring: Zhou Chun-bo's Son, a Young Hostage, in Pudong; French Police Dispatch Detectives to Consult with Public Security Bureau for Search; Maid Jin Zhou with Suspicion

Zhou Chun-bo from Hubei, residing at No. 135 Bubbling Well Road, French Concession, has been working at a local exchange for years and has some assets. Zhou has two sons, the elder named Jie-sheng, only four years old, and the younger still an infant. On the 4th of this month, at around 1:00 PM, the maid Jin Zhou, a Shaoxing native (43 years old), who had been employed for six years, took the elder son Jie-sheng to play at the doorway. Suddenly, a strange car came, and several bandits jumped out, kidnapping Jin Zhou and Jie-sheng onto the car and speeding away. When the Zhou family learned of this, they urgently reported to the police, who dispatched detectives to pursue them, but they were already gone. The next day, the Zhou family received a letter delivered by the post office. After reading the contents, they were certain that it was sent by the bandits, only informing them that the hostage was safe, without setting a ransom. For over ten days since then, they have not received a second ransom demand. Yesterday afternoon, the Old Zha Police Station of the Public Concession arrested a bandit named Xu Ren-gui at a certain location, who confessed that his accomplices were hiding in a new bungalow at No. 12 Peide Lane, near Shiditang, West Yangjiazhai, Pudong. At 6:30 PM, detectives You A-gen and Lu Gen-sheng, along with Western Detective Bodé, of the police station took the criminal to the Pudong Public Security Bureau, requesting assistance in the apprehension. The bureau chief Zhang Ming-qin immediately dispatched over ten police officers to the location, surrounding it front and back. They immediately searched the room and discovered that the so-called hideout was actually a kidnapping ring. The hostage being held was Zhou Chun-bo's kidnapped elder son, Jie-sheng. Bandits Zhang Xi-biao (41 years old, Shaoxing native), Jin Feng-xiang (38 years old, Shaoxing native), Ma Liang-fu (34 years old, Shaoxing native), Wang Shi-pin (Shaoxing native), and woman Wang Xie (36 years old, Shaoxing native), girl Wang Xiang-zhen (18 years old, Shaoxing native), boy Wang Xiang-cao (13 years old, Shaoxing native), and seven other people were arrested. Zhou Chun-bo's maid, Jin Zhou, and the hostage Zhou Jie-sheng, were also in the house. A Mauser pistol with serial number 454142 and 17 bullets were also confiscated. All the people were taken to the Pudong Bureau for questioning. It was found that Zhou's maid, Jin Zhou, was from the same place as the bandits, and there was a strong suspicion of her involvement. The fingerprinted suspects were then taken to the police station by detectives Zhang Zi-ying and others of the French Concession police for disposal. The Pudong Bureau found that the house was rented by Xi and Wang from the landlord on the 8th of this month, and there was a guarantor. The police were sent to guard the house and reported to the superiors, awaiting instructions on how to handle the matter.

New Sports Association: Convening a Meeting of Prison Staff to Discuss and Resolve Issues Such as Improving Prison Hygiene

The New Sports Association of this city convened a discussion meeting yesterday (the 17th) with representatives from various courts, command headquarters, public security bureaus, and other agencies in the city. Those present included Shi Zhonghe from the Second Special District Local Court, Zhu Xinrong from the Jiangsu Second Branch Prison, Dong Chongshan from the Jiangsu High Second Branch Court, Xie Shuming from the Jiangsu High Third Branch Court, Wu Fengcan from the Shanghai Local Court, Zhang Tianfu from the Shanghai First Special District Local Court, Han Wenqing from the Public Security Bureau, Lu Jingshi from the Command Headquarters, Zhang Shouyao, Jiang Hao, Zhu Jiarang, and Shen Liangzhong from the New Sports Association. Zhang Shou was the chairman, and Zhu Jiarang was the recording secretary. The chairman first gave a report, followed by discussions and resolutions on eleven items: accuracy of court hearing times; law enforcement officers versus guards; neatness of uniforms; orderliness within the courtroom during hearings; law enforcement officers' and guards' attitude towards prisoners should be peaceful; cleanliness inside the prison and the warden's office; hygiene issues related to prisoner meals; toilets should be established in detention centers and prisons; regular free haircuts and baths should be provided to prisoners, and strictly followed; prisoners should be vaccinated against smallpox and receive preventative injections; law enforcement officers and prison guards are strictly prohibited from extorting tips; cleanliness within the office.

Expansion of the Second Branch of the High Court

The Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court has expanded its premises. Due to the limited space of the original location, which was insufficient for its needs, the court purchased over ten rooms in the Xipuyi Lane adjacent to the court last winter. Since the buildings were not very old, they were slightly renovated. The renovation is now complete, and some staff members have moved into the new space to alleviate overcrowding. Previously, the Second Branch of the High Court only had one civil court and one criminal court. Now, the room in front of the First Court, which was formerly a lounge for lawyers, has been converted into a Third Court, and the room next to the Revenue and Expenditure Office has been vacated to serve as the lawyers' lounge. Currently, the Second Branch of the High Court has three courtrooms. It is rumored that another courtroom will be opened in the newly purchased building, so there will be no shortage of venues for trials in the future.

Public Concession, March: Overview of Public Works Department Activities

According to the Public Works Department's report for March, the Chengdu Road police station residence was handed over to the police department for use during the month. The installation of electrical and sanitary equipment at the Rongqin Road quarantine station has been completed. Machines and other equipment are currently being installed. Cement for the fire escape of the Peng Road Chinese Children's School has been poured up to the first floor, and the strengthening of the floors is underway. Regarding garbage, a total of 1,277 tons of household waste and 326 tons of street waste were transported to the east and west districts by freight cars for landfill. In addition, 2,982 tons of garbage were transported by small vehicles. Contractors transported 19,512 tons of household waste and 720 tons of street waste by boat to other locations. 1,299 tons were transported to Maohai Road for incineration, and 2,991 tons were transported to Binlang Road for incineration. Furthermore, there were 201 houses under construction during the month. 183 applications for building plans were submitted for approval, and 88 were approved. 79 houses were appraised for tax collection. A total of 6,149 house inspections were conducted.

The quota is set at 20 people, and the cost is 184 yuan per person, including round-trip second-class train tickets, transportation, meals, accommodation, and all sightseeing expenses. The journey from Shanghai to Beijing and back will be made on direct military trains. Berths and meals will be specially arranged by the travel agency in advance with the railway bureau, ensuring comfort and luxury. All rooms and meals in the above-mentioned accommodations are of the highest quality, unlike other casual arrangements. Weather Report

The weather forecast from the Xujiahui Observatory at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: The weather between the Yellow Sea and the Yangtze River is cloudy, with localized rain. A cyclone, due to low pressure, is moving towards the northeast-east. The upper reaches of the Yangtze River are overcast or rainy. There is a south to southwest wind here, with some clearing in the afternoon. The south to southeast wind in the East China Sea is quite strong. Furthermore, in the 24 hours prior to 2 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in the city was 67.2 degrees, and the lowest was 58.1 degrees. Last year on the same day, the highest temperature was 58.1 degrees, and the lowest was 50.2 degrees.

Sino-British International Billiards: Chinese Still Hold the Advantage. Results from the Second Day Show a Lead of 34 Points. Hu Changyuan Lost by 125 Points Yesterday.

The results of the second day of competition in the Fourth Sino-British International Billiards Tournament show that the Chinese team still holds the advantage, leading by 34 points. The third match, Shen Lince versus Bockell, will be held next Monday (the 20th) at 5:30 PM. The competition for the championship is becoming increasingly intense, and the outcome depends on the result of the third match.

Fighting Hard Against a Strong Opponent: Yesterday, Hu Changyuan maintained a serious attitude and a determined will, battling the Englishman Clark for three hours. The number of points he lost was not as high as expected. He not only fulfilled his duty but also inspired the spirit of the Chinese team. From the ninth shot onwards, Hu had a cumulative lead, and by the thirtieth shot, the score was 144 to 125, giving him a lead of 19 points. Clark had a stroke of luck, scoring unexpected points and launching an offensive. Unfortunately, Hu inadvertently shot the ball out of bounds and had to stop. Otherwise, he would have won by more than just 27 points. Later, both sides competed on the central horizontal line, and by the forty-fourth shot, Hu Changyuan still had a one-point lead at 256 to 125.

Following the Rules: After the forty-fifth shot, Clark gradually improved, and his shots were on target. He scored two short scores of 32 and 37 in a row (the highest score of the day), resulting in a difference of over 80 points. In the end, he scored another 32 points, exceeding 100 points. Hu Changyuan used the strategy of clearing the field to resist his strong opponent, but due to Clark's all-around skills, he could only helplessly try to recover points. As a result, Hu Changyuan lost by 125 points with a score of 485 to 600. Clark's high scores were 27, 20, 32, 37, 32, and 21, while Hu Changyuan's were 20, 25, 22, 25, 24, and 27.

Jiangnan University Volleyball Tournament to Commence on the 29th

The regulations for the 9th Jiangnan University Volleyball Championship have been announced as follows:

* Date: The tournament will commence on April 29th and conclude on May 6th.

* Competition: The competition method will adopt a single round-robin system.

* Rules: The tournament will be conducted in accordance with the latest volleyball rules reviewed and approved by the National Sports Association.

* Referee: The home team is responsible for engaging referees designated by the Chinese Referee Association.

* Registration: Registration must be submitted to the Chairman of the Volleyball Committee (Shen Kunnan at Yinan University of Medicine) one day before the start of the tournament.

* Time: Women's matches will begin at 2:00 PM, and men's matches will begin at 3:00 PM.

* Scoring: In each match, the winning team will receive two points, and the losing team will receive zero points. The team with the most points will win the championship.

Education News

Universities Enrolling New Students; Ministry of Education Issues Order for Restrictions; Next Year's Method Will Follow This Year's Method

(Nanjing, 17th dispatch) The Ministry of Education issued an order that for the 25th year, all universities and independent colleges enrolling new and transfer students will, unless otherwise stipulated by the Ministry for specific departments or colleges that have been ordered to suspend enrollment of new students within a limited time, continue to apply the enrollment methods of the 24th year. Key points: 1. All departments of arts, law, commerce, education, science, agriculture, medicine, and engineering in all universities and independent colleges should carefully examine the qualifications of teachers and equipment conditions of each department and determine the number of students to be enrolled in each department to ensure that teaching efficiency is actually achieved. There should be no excessive enrollment. 2. Universities with colleges of arts, law, commerce, and education, and independent colleges with departments of arts, law, commerce, and education, should limit the number of new and transfer students enrolled in each department or specialized course to 30, unless special circumstances such as outstanding academic performance have been specifically authorized by the Ministry before the enrollment. Universities with colleges of arts and science, or independent colleges with departments of arts and science, should also follow the provisions of this item for each department or specialized course belonging to arts, law, commerce, and education. Universities with colleges of science, agriculture, engineering, and medicine, or independent colleges with departments of science, agriculture, engineering, and medicine, which have affiliated departments or specialized courses of arts, law, commerce, and education, should also follow the provisions of this item for their enrollment methods. 3. Schools that do not enroll students in accordance with these methods will not have the enrollment qualifications of their new and transfer students approved by the Ministry. 4. These regulations do not apply to colleges that specialize in female students for the time being.

The Educational Inspection Report of Superintendent Zhou of Anhui Province's Education (1)

According to the inspection report of Superintendent Zhou Bangdao, Anhui Province's education has many outstanding aspects, such as the unified control of the construction and equipment of provincial schools, the organization of the provincial education supplies consumer cooperative, the subsidizing of outstanding students from poor families, the establishment of local education supervisors, the implementation of the normal school guidance area, the exceeding of the original plan for the number of short-term primary schools established, the pilot implementation of the guidance student system and the teaching student system, and the rectification of training in private schools and secondary schools. However, there are still points that need to be improved, which are recorded below.

I. Regarding Compulsory Education:

Each county should appoint a chief of the joint guarantee within five to ten primary school districts as the school director of that school district. Due to the relationship between the position and authority of the chief of the joint guarantee, it is relatively easy to complete the tasks stipulated in Article 29 of the Implementation Rules of the Outline of the Provisional Measures for the Implementation of Compulsory Education. However, the qualifications, knowledge, sense of responsibility, and location of residence of the chief of the joint guarantee must be carefully considered before appointment, so that it is easy to be effective and not equal to a formality. If necessary, guidance or assistant personnel may be appointed in accordance with the provisions of the same article to guide or assist the school director in handling affairs. As the school director is originally an unpaid voluntary position, efforts should be made to encourage them spiritually to avoid neglecting the basic work of compulsory education due to the lack of material rewards.

The number of short-term primary school students in each county is relatively small. Setting up only one class per school is uneconomical and does not fully meet the original purpose of the central government's promotion of compulsory education. In the future, in addition to ordering the principals of each short-term primary school to strictly implement the "Methods for Enrolling and Retaining Students" in the "Short-Term Primary School Principal's Guide," the compulsory enrollment methods that have been announced should be strictly enforced to achieve practical results.

Administrative personnel in charge of compulsory education in each county should formulate performance appraisal methods, conduct detailed assessments, and strictly impose rewards and punishments.

The methods of the Xuan City Short-Term Primary School Award Association and the Wuhu special short-term primary school teacher substitute class method are of great help to the promotion of compulsory education and should be followed in each county within a possible range.

The number of short-term primary school teachers in the province is quite lacking. The short-term primary school teacher training class should be organized as soon as possible in accordance with the 25th year overall planning for staffing short-term primary schools, and the art friend system should be implemented to make it easier for students to be trained and to distribute teachers universally. In addition to Fuyang, Huangli, and Huizhou, teachers should be designated elsewhere. It seems that the treatment should be slightly higher in order to stabilize their lives.

Some short-term primary schools in each county have people who hold other positions and are distracted by outside affairs, some are nominally running the school but privately ask others to take their place, and some do not enroll students but hang the school sign at private schools and give the private school teachers a certain amount of subsidy. Such situations should be investigated and dealt with to warn against emulation.

Students and their parents in short-term primary schools in each county are mostly dissatisfied with the half-day two-part system. Schools with sufficient school buildings and equipment should set up more two-part systems with questions, or mixed two-part systems. For those with few students, ordinary complex compilation can be used, and direct teaching and indirect teaching can be used to allocate students so that students can be in school all day. However, complex teaching methods must be specially studied in order to be used freely.

In order to adapt to the different levels of short-term primary school students, supplementary teaching materials can be given to those with stronger learning abilities and those who still request to study after graduation. All new and old readings from elementary schools and public schools, or commonly used texts circulating in the market, can be adopted as appropriate without restriction. The source of such materials can be purchased by students' parents or raised from donations. If teachers lack the ability to teach phonetic symbols, it seems that they can be temporarily suspended to avoid wasting time.

Difficulties arise and abuses emerge from the fact that the opening equipment and office expenses of short-term primary schools in each county are raised and designated by the chiefs of the joint guarantee. It is urgent to find ways to improve them. Xiuning plans to be planned and coordinated by the county government, and Wuhu plans to use the method of unified collection and expenditure, which are both worth referring to.

The salaries of short-term primary school teachers in each county, except for those who personally receive them in nearby places, can be sent to the schools or other designated places on a monthly basis by the county education bureau, with receipts being drawn up. The public expense is limited, but the short-term primary school teachers save a lot of time and money, which is a great benefit. (To be continued)

National Children's Painting Exhibition; The Opening Date Is Approaching and Preparations Are Actively Underway

The Sixth Preparatory Meeting Was Held Yesterday to Telegraph Various Provinces and Cities to Urge Submission of Works; The Method for Soliciting Painters' Works on Oral Arts Education and Writings Was Passed

The National Children's Painting Exhibition held its sixth preparatory meeting at the Municipal Education Bureau conference room at 10:00 AM yesterday. Pan Gong (Hu Shuyi representing), Chen Heqin, Hu Shuyi, Chen Tiesheng, Chen Huifan, Qian Fugong, Kechang, Zhou Wanghe (Qian representing), and Ma Gongyu (representing) attended, and Qian Honglie attended as an observer. Chen Heqin chaired the meeting, and Qian Honglie recorded the minutes.

Key Issues Decided at the Sixth Preparatory Meeting: Regarding the question of how to print the association's publicity manual, it was resolved to allocate funds for printing from the association's preparatory expenses, and to solicit advertisements at the same time to provide support. The General Affairs Section will handle this. Since the deadline for submissions is approaching, should letters be sent directly to various provinces and cities to urge them to send works? It was resolved that in addition to requesting the National Children's Association Implementation Committee to forward a request to the Ministry of Education to issue an urging order, the association will directly telegraph various provinces and cities to urge submissions. The Collection and Editing Section will handle this. Since it is more convenient for children in Shanghai to participate in the painting competition, should a letter be sent directly to the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau to instruct schools to actively participate? It was resolved that the association will directly send a letter requesting them to do so. The motion to send a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau to stipulate a method for schools to take turns visiting was passed. The motion to determine the method of displaying the exhibits was approved. It was resolved that the judges and the display section should quickly consult and formulate a plan and immediately convene a joint meeting to discuss the progress together. Committees Kechang and Sun Yi will be handed over to the Public Relations and Disciplinary Sections to handle together, and a joint meeting will be convened immediately, convened by Committee Member Chen Zhengfan and Committee Member Zhou Wang. The motion to compile and print a special opening issue was resolved to be handled by Committee Member Qian Fugong. The motion to commission a children's newspaper to publish a special issue at the venue was resolved to be published by the Children's Morning Post, and Committee Member Hu Shuyi will contact them. The motion to pass the method of soliciting the works of families was passed and it was resolved to hand it over to the Collection and Editing Section for active handling. The motion to pass the method of collecting art education theses was passed and it was resolved to hand it over to the Collection and Editing Section to handle. The motion to determine the method of soliciting advertisements for the venue was resolved to hand it over to the General Affairs Section to handle. The motion to send a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Children's Film Promotion Committee to screen films during the exhibition period was passed. The motion to stipulate the opening ceremony program was resolved to be handled by the General Affairs Section. All the members of the committee went to the municipal stadium to survey the exhibition venue (the buildings around the track and field) and conducted extensive discussions on the design of the layout and display. According to the buildings at the venue, which are spacious and grand, can accommodate more than 100,000 people, the lively situation of the National Games will be re-posted on June 6.

Method for Soliciting Painters' Works: In order to enhance children's ability to appreciate art and their interest in art, the association specially solicits painters' works in accordance with this method. The scope of solicitation for the above-mentioned works is as follows: 1. Brush paintings, 2. Crayon paintings, 3. Pencil drawings, 4. Chalk paintings, 5. Watercolor paintings, 6. Wood ash paintings, 7. Pattern paintings, 8. Others. There are no regulations on the size and dimensions of the above-mentioned works. If the above-mentioned works need to be decorated, it shall be handled by the exhibitor himself. After the above-mentioned works are collected, the association will specially display them in a special room during the exhibition period. After the above-mentioned works are collected, in addition to the exhibitor voluntarily donating them as prizes for children's works, the rest will be returned by the association. All solicited works must be sent to the association's preparatory committee (transferred through the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau) before May 25, 25th year. This method shall be announced and implemented after being approved by the association's preparatory committee and shall be sent to the National Children's Year Implementation Committee for record.

Deputy Director Liu, Section Chief Dong, the representative of the commissioner, and Ren Xingbing of the military school's special party department delivered speeches one after another, with many encouragements. At the end, You Shichao, a student of the class, delivered a reply on behalf of the students. After the ceremony, the guests from various provinces were led by the reception staff of the zone to visit the zone's public basic school, the rural agricultural class dormitory, the Lv Miao cooperative, and the exhibits of the rural agricultural achievements, administrative achievements, and staff achievements, which were arranged in an extremely orderly manner, and the audience praised them very much.

Yesterday in the Guest Xian rice market, arrivals came from various ports along the Yangtze River and eastern Zhejiang, but volumes were low, while demand was strong. The sluggish market showed signs of recovery. If local merchants and guest wholesalers continue to buy, prices may rise gradually. Although local rice supplies are sufficient, foreign rice transport remains difficult. Trading remains quiet as both sides maintain their positions. Local sales of Guest Xian rice were decent yesterday, and buyers were making inquiries. There is hope for a turnaround in the market. Daily transactions included 2,000 bags of Jiangxi rice, 540 bags of Wenzhou-Taizhou rice, 1,750 bags of Jiangbei rice, 161 bags of Anhui rice, and 340 bags of Hunan rice. Prices remained similar to the previous day.

River Rice Rebounds Slightly

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the number of suppliers remained at just over 30, with a total supply of over 6,000 dan. The market was initially weak but tightened later. Bao Wei of Tianjin only purchased over 1,000 bags. As a result, the price of thick early japonica rice increased by 0.10 USD, and paddy rice also tightened. Du Yang pointed rice remained similar, and Yin Bian Yuan was stable.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, 36 or 37 boats arrived from various areas along the river. Sales were brisk in the market, and retail sales continued. Bao Wei of Tianjin rice moved slightly, and the market tightened by several fen to over 0.10 USD. Early rice followed closely, tightening by nearly 0.10 USD. Sales of thin rice remained sluggish, and prices were stable. Yang Du pointed rice continued to see retail sales, and prices tightened by a few fen. Port customers held firm on pointed rice, and Yin Bian Yuan was stable. Prices for other varieties showed a tendency to increase.
